  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_961bac1d-5e6c-45d0-b095-e80e194e420c'
      });

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think Goodreads Giveaways are for real paperback copies, not eBooks.<br/><br/>At the top menu, Click "Browse"--> Giveaways --> List a Giveaway<br/><br/>Then provide the<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think Goodreads Giveaways are for real paperback copies, not eBooks.<br /><br />At the top menu, Click "Browse"--&gt; Giveaways --&gt; List a Giveaway<br /><br />Then provide the details of the book, and the duration of the giveaway. The Giveaway will typically go live in a week's time. Once it ends, GoodReads will send you an email and you can go to the Giveaway page and see the winners and their addresses. You can order books for them directly online or send copies yourself.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1736679390" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736679390" />
    <a title="Archit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54103953-archit"><img alt="Archit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526805090p2/54103953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736679390?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Archit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Archit" href="/user/show/54103953-archit">Archit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54103953-archit?shelf=copies-from-publishers-and-authors">copies-from-publishers-and-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54103953-archit?shelf=books-we-own">books-we-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736679390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14832753563432063870"><b>
  <i> <s>Thrilled.</s> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457908369ra/18421363.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Bewitched, captivated and mesmerized by the beauty of it! Seriously. </i>
</b><br/><br/>Well, to begin with :<br/><br/><b>My assumptions <u>before</u> reading the book : </b><br/><br/>It is a mystery and thriller novel with the detective named<i> Coinman </i>(similar to James Bond, Detective Gopichand etc. ). He is going to solve crimes, murders and cases never seen solved before! Criminals will shiver hearing just his name! He is the God of the city!!!<br/><br/>The cover itself shows that some bigger racket is going on under police's nose but Coinm</span>
  <span id="freeText14832753563432063870" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> <s>Thrilled.</s> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457908369ra/18421363.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bewitched, captivated and mesmerized by the beauty of it! Seriously. </i>
</b><br><br>Well, to begin with :<br><br><b>My assumptions <u>before</u> reading the book : </b><br><br>It is a mystery and thriller novel with the detective named<i> Coinman </i>(similar to James Bond, Detective Gopichand etc. ). He is going to solve crimes, murders and cases never seen solved before! Criminals will shiver hearing just his name! He is the God of the city!!!<br><br>The cover itself shows that some bigger racket is going on under police's nose but Coinman will be ultimate and overshadow all the detectives born before! <br><br><i>Hail Coinman!!!</i><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Reality: </b>
</u><br><br>I've no words in my mind to tell you how superb <b>Coinman</b> is!! <br><br>One thing you should know, it is NOT a mystery book, it is MORE than this! <br><br>Other than being honest, a cry baby, obedient, having TOO-much-good-to-everyone attitude and no-friends-at-all-man, his only major, visible and AUDIBLE characteristic is, that the protagonist, Coinman loves the sound of coin jingling!! <br><br>That's it! <br><br>That's very much it!<br><br>And if you are thinking, like I did, that how can someone come up with a story about this good-for-nothing guy! How can a story even exist about this useless person!!<br><br>Then, <b>you are SO SO wrong, mi amigo!! </b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14594440.Pawan_Mishra" title="Pawan Mishra" rel="nofollow noopener">Pawan Mishra</a> has nailed it!<br><br>Not only he speaks eloquently to readers about the adventurous, unique and honest world of Coinman with vividness and genius intensity but also he makes you feel that you see a Coinman everyday in your office, bus stops and streets until you, yourself become a Coinman!<br><br>Everyone in his office is one way or other familiar to you. They are people who love to gossip and that's their life! Hukum, Panna, Sevak, Shimla, Imli, Keshar and Andar, Bandar, Chandar! Tell me, how are you to resist laughing when you have characters with these names!?!<br><br>Ratiram's "Coin" was ultimate of all of them!!<br><br>Like all my other reviews, I'll tell you where I had to put down the book and laugh for a really long time! For me, it was when Coinman's wife, Imli, thinks, (yes, thinks) that "I'm a stranger!" <br><br><i>(Read the book, come back to this line and you'll know why!) </i><br><br><b> Verdict: this is THE book, my friend. </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473352935i/20452572._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> P.S. I would have written much more, but it's time for my coin-jingling session! Coinman's addiction, you see! </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14832753563432063870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1715607929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1715607929" />
    <a title="Pooja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30059190-pooja"><img alt="Pooja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495711105p2/30059190.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1715607929?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pooja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pooja" href="/user/show/30059190-pooja">Pooja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who want to laugh </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30059190-pooja?shelf=100-pages">100-pages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30059190-pooja?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1715607929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17913681386704015188">You can never imagine what human minds are capable of!<br/><br/>Thoroughly enjoyed it!<br/><br/>You hardly expect any book to be as enchanting as this.<br/><br/>Let me tell you, the characters are super duper simple, real-life ones and extremely likable. <br/>Coinman is a person you meet or see in a day to day life. He sits with you. He talks to you and you don't behave well with him. Yes, he's that tragic person. What it's like to hear his story? You better find it out reading it. <br/><br/>Why Coinman? Couldn't the author come up with an</span>
  <span id="freeText17913681386704015188" style="display:none">You can never imagine what human minds are capable of!<br /><br />Thoroughly enjoyed it!<br /><br />You hardly expect any book to be as enchanting as this.<br /><br />Let me tell you, the characters are super duper simple, real-life ones and extremely likable. <br />Coinman is a person you meet or see in a day to day life. He sits with you. He talks to you and you don't behave well with him. Yes, he's that tragic person. What it's like to hear his story? You better find it out reading it. <br /><br />Why Coinman? Couldn't the author come up with any other name? <br /><br />A Big NO!! Coinman, in my opinion, is the best chosen name ever for a character like in this book. He loves to jingle coins. He can't help it. He loves the sound of the coins, colliding with each other. Oh My, would you ever think in your entire life that a novel can be written on a person of this kind?<br /><br />At least I never thought so. Narration, theme, setting, characters : Everything at their bests!<br /><br />I enjoy too much drama in a book, how some people bully the protagonist and in the end he overcomes his troubles. Well, Coinman : An Untold Conspiracy was much more than entertainment. <br /><br />It has been written with humorous punches (Warning : They hit you hard!), a sarcastic tone looming over every sentence and a fantastic set. I was completely arrested to this book and its narration. <br /><br />Books like Coinman are infrequent to find. This book is nothing less than a trophy for the literary arena. I highly recommend it. <br />I congratulate the author for picking up the most common character we can imagine and making him a superhero! A Coinman!<br /><br />Fabulously narrated and one of the most entertaining novel that I ask you to not miss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17913681386704015188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17044931255229752453">In the book "Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy" by Pawan Mishra, In the story, we meet the main character Kesar who because of his obsession with the coins becomes Coinman.   <span id="freeText17044931255229752453" style="display:none">In the book "Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy" by Pawan Mishra, In the story, we meet the main character Kesar who because of his obsession with the coins becomes Coinman. But his whole life was a tangle of various events that the condition to become the way it is. His mother and father are full of love for him but also those directed him throughout his life, holding all the strings in his hands. His father and mother take responsibility for his education, work, and marriage. He listens to the decision of their parents and respects their demands and accepts what they want. But if this is what they want does not matter, because it must be so. Jingling coins which rotate in its pocket is the only thing he loves. It relaxes and soothes, but people view him with suspicion. But in this world, if you were different this immediately causes gossip that people invent things that have nothing to do with the truth. Gossip on his work slowly but surely becoming so branched that their makers are gathering in the cafeteria where a wider and eventually culminates in consequences for all participants. The writer Pawan Mishra, the story takes us steady hand showing us through Coinman lifetime reasons why he is the way he is. The writer very good describing draws us into the story in order to understand the reasons why some characters are as they are. Personally, I liked the book and I'd like to recommend to readers who love a good book, and that this book is.<br />My rating is 4.5 out of 5.</span>

<div id="review_1693294867" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1693294867" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1693294867?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=traditional-fiction">traditional-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1693294867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7464539017285720764">Thanks to the author for allowing me to review his book!<br/><br/>This one is a fairly difficult book to review, because while certain elements were dong very well, the book didn't stay within the lines of how it began, how it progressed, or how it ended. It started out as a pretty funny Milton-like office satire, with tons of details that really showed us how horrible the corporate world is in bright and shiny satire.<br/><br/>The way the Coinman was shown to us, I was frankly expecting this to turn into a fantasy</span>
  <span id="freeText7464539017285720764" style="display:none">Thanks to the author for allowing me to review his book!<br /><br />This one is a fairly difficult book to review, because while certain elements were dong very well, the book didn't stay within the lines of how it began, how it progressed, or how it ended. It started out as a pretty funny Milton-like office satire, with tons of details that really showed us how horrible the corporate world is in bright and shiny satire.<br /><br />The way the Coinman was shown to us, I was frankly expecting this to turn into a fantasy where the coins jingling in his pockets annoying all his coworkers would turn into some sort of magical realism, and especially when they ganged up on him and made his life a living hell, I rather hoped for some sort of dire revenge or a setup for a greater fall for Coinman, himself.<br /><br />But no. Instead, the novel became a pretty decent setup for a horror novel, with Coinman's early life, troubles, social isolation, obsessions, and a number of truly pathos-inducing incidents that make him what he is in the modern Office-Space. I felt the dire-build-up. I felt like we were headed toward tragedy town, with Coinman being the tragic hero. The novel set up me up for a few anxiety attacks. Hell, perhaps there should be a trigger warning on the novel for people who are introverted and isolated. By this point, I wanted some serious resolution in a positive way for the man.<br /><br />But then, the novel took another turn and we got to know his wife, his home situation, and things only get worse for him. <br /><br />Where's the satire? Well, it's there, still plowing away at us and it's still good, but the humor has given way to sadness, and I'm not entirely sure that the novel worked well for me at this point.<br /><br />The whole office conspiracy was a pretty good setup, and I did eventually like Coinman, even if he was a very flawed individual, and each of the elemental setups were good by themselves, but they were promises that weren't really filled by the end of the tale.<br /><br />In this respect, it's more of a mainstream novel. Maybe a bit arty. Let you make up your own mind who's the hero or even if there was one at all. Unfortunately, it's not really my kind of thing.<br /><br />Fortunately, I was never really bored by the book, though, even if the ultimate satisfaction wasn't there.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7464539017285720764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1569577000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1569577000" />
    <a title="Nelou Keramati" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49578594-nelou-keramati"><img alt="Nelou Keramati" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546917844p2/49578594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1569577000?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nelou Keramati" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nelou Keramati" href="/user/show/49578594-nelou-keramati">Nelou Keramati</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1569577000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15486552074281399246">Refreshingly unique, humorous, and honest!<br/><br/>As someone who is predominantly drawn to the YA/NA/Fantasy/Paranormal/Sci-Fi genres, reading literary fiction was indeed a departure from the norm. With that said, I found the underlying dynamics of <i>Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy</i> to be a rather accurate satirical representation of contemporary life. Although I am neither terribly familiar with office politics, nor with living in India, I found Coinman to be a highly relevant tale concerned with addressing</span>
  <span id="freeText15486552074281399246" style="display:none">Refreshingly unique, humorous, and honest!<br /><br />As someone who is predominantly drawn to the YA/NA/Fantasy/Paranormal/Sci-Fi genres, reading literary fiction was indeed a departure from the norm. With that said, I found the underlying dynamics of <i>Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy</i> to be a rather accurate satirical representation of contemporary life. Although I am neither terribly familiar with office politics, nor with living in India, I found Coinman to be a highly relevant tale concerned with addressing the darker aspects of human nature. Kesar’s (a.k.a. Coinman’s) obsessive attachment to his coins, and the subsequent rousing antagonism from his co-workers (who are incapable of understanding/unwilling to tolerate it) are masterfully depicted, and perfectly balanced with the author’s sense of humor.<br /><br />The prose itself is a plethora of memorable quotes, but I would argue that Mishra’s eloquent writing style is itself a feast for lovers of literary fiction:<br /><br />“Disappointment has quite a penchant for taking one by surprise.”<br /><br />“The pristine spiritual atmosphere was ideal for immersion in one’s true soul and spending time in its rejuvenation.”<br /><br />This also means that Coinman is not a lazy read. The author has pored over every single word in this novel. No sentences are throwaways, and few of them read at a fast pace because of the author’s rich descriptive style:<br /><br />“The loss of a reliance on others often helpfully forces a more sophisticated rumination that enables opening of previously unknown avenues.”<br /><br />If reading in order to get from A to B, the reader is bound to find him/herself in a state of confusion. Mishra’s words are not of the kind one can gloss over. They are intelligent and contemplative, often with multiple meanings and layers that allow for more than basic interpretation, but encourage perspective as well. In conjunction with the powerful themes of identity and intolerance, I feel that regardless of one’s cultural background, marital status, or occupation, readers of all walks of life can deeply relate to this story!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15486552074281399246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1497762565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497762565" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1497762565?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=literary-fiction-love">literary-fiction-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=humorous-hysteria">humorous-hysteria</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=satirical-susceptiveness">satirical-susceptiveness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1497762565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14638526083507821022">I received this book in exchange for an honest review. Thanks to the author, Pawan Mishra, and the publisher,Lune Spark LLC, for providing me with a copy.<br/><br/>I can honestly say that this book is unlike any other I have read before. Whilst reading, the first two notes I made were “curioser and curioser” and “is the Mad Hatter our protagonist!?”. This book started, in a word, oddly. But it was odd in the most wonderful and fantastical sense. I loved the personal manner used when addressing the reader,</span>
  <span id="freeText14638526083507821022" style="display:none">I received this book in exchange for an honest review. Thanks to the author, Pawan Mishra, and the publisher,Lune Spark LLC, for providing me with a copy.<br /><br />I can honestly say that this book is unlike any other I have read before. Whilst reading, the first two notes I made were “curioser and curioser” and “is the Mad Hatter our protagonist!?”. This book started, in a word, oddly. But it was odd in the most wonderful and fantastical sense. I loved the personal manner used when addressing the reader, I loved the sardonic and humorous tone, and I loved that straight away I was borne away on the story. I had little idea of what was going on, but that was okay: to be a part of it was enough. I did, however, find it initially jarring to feel so totally lost in the world presented to me and dually find it totally recognisable for its contemporary and realistic setting. It felt like two genres has collided and left this medley in its wake. And I think it was a success! Although it did take some getting used to, this book wasn’t set out in the typical forward-motion timeline, and the beginning, middle and end felt like they had been stirred together. Over time, this proved to be part of the book’s overall appeal.<br /><br /><i> Coinman </i> is the story of Kesar, whose bad workplace etiquette, in reference to his incessant pocket coin-jingling, leads to alienation and isolation from his peers and the subsequent loss of his identity; forevermore to be referred to, as the title suggests, as Coinman. Quite a simple premise, really. What wasn’t simple was the multitude of perspectives and angles offered to the reader, the time frame that dipped between past and present and the varied insights into the home, social and work life of multiple characters. All of which combined to muddy the waters of the good guys/bad guys binaries and keep me at a total loss of where the story was going. In short, what I learned was that nothing is quite as it seems in this book…<br /><br />The characters each have distinctive traits, so enhanced as to almost appear as caricatures. This, I believe, was a deliberate stylistic approach from the author to heighten the discord between characters and the satirical angle of the book. If the characters were larger than life, then the tales they conjured about Coinman’s habits outside of work were even more fantastic. These tales were nothing more than fancy, but it was these fancies that fuelled the work cliche's hatred for Coinman and kept them from internalising any of these feelings onto their own innate flaws (they had many) or focusing too closely on the unlikability of each other.<br /><br />Amidst all the satire and hilarity, it wasn’t hard to remember that this book was just a more obvious and heightened version of exactly what occurs in many workplaces. The gang mentality instanced here wasn’t an isolated, fantastical occurrence and I felt the book morphed into a didactic outlook on the events occurring, despite never claiming partiality for either ‘side’. The workplace bullying instanced was horrific and, despite being an unlikely hero, I found myself continually in Coinman’s corner. He clearly has issues of his own – his personification and affinity towards his beloved coins, as though they were living, breathing things with wills and whims of their own and his social anxiety and awkwardness – which did not always make him the most likable person, but the warmth I felt for him stemmed from his treatment by others. My affinity for this antihero continued to grow, and my emotional investment in his welfare was only ever heightened as more and more character flaws of his were revealed, embellished or artificially created. Long live Coinman!<br /> <br />Would I have chosen this book based on synopsis, if not provided for me by the author? Honestly? Probably not. The synopsis betrayed little that immediately grabbed my attention and I was more curious than captivated. I was totally unprepared for the U-Turn my feelings would take. I feel completely grateful that I was given the opportunity to read outside of my preferred genres and comfort zones and to find that I actually love it! I think the overall message here, in reference to the book and Coinman himself, is that different doesn’t always equate to bad.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14638526083507821022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

For me, that's the true test of a great book! I will definitely be reading it again. Bravo!</span>

<div id="review_1726659632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1726659632?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan Hagan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan Hagan" href="/user/show/58006459-susan-hagan">Susan Hagan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1726659632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12559752322815754645">Very few books are written once. This is one of those books. Most of the books I read, except for the classic stories or the different books that come out once in a while, have something or the other that I would have read somewhere else.<br/><br/>As I started the book, I was a bit lost on the first page, but since the writing was wonderful, I kept going for on the promise of intelligent writing. It was very soon that I fell in love with the writing: every word, every sentence I read seemed to be refined </span>
  <span id="freeText12559752322815754645" style="display:none">Very few books are written once. This is one of those books. Most of the books I read, except for the classic stories or the different books that come out once in a while, have something or the other that I would have read somewhere else.<br /><br />As I started the book, I was a bit lost on the first page, but since the writing was wonderful, I kept going for on the promise of intelligent writing. It was very soon that I fell in love with the writing: every word, every sentence I read seemed to be refined very thoroughly. And the story, the plot, the characters? They were so wonderfully original that I wanted to deliberately go slow to thoroughly enjoy the book. The book is so well written, and carries such an elegant &amp; sophisticated way of storytelling that it should belong in the libraries as text book example for creative writing.<br /><br />Now on the not so nice part. I don't think the book is for everyone. Definitely not for readers, we have plenty today, who read to increase the count of books they have read, who want to finish a book in a day by browsing through writings that lack substance. This book has to be savored slow to understand two or three layers of wit, sarcasm, and humor. Most readers today turn to books as they turn to fast food. So I am not sure everyone would like this book. </span>

<div id="review_1480384782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1480384782" />
    <a title="Pankaj Goyal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7934176-pankaj-goyal"><img alt="Pankaj Goyal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539426057p2/7934176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1480384782?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pankaj Goyal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pankaj Goyal" href="/user/show/7934176-pankaj-goyal">Pankaj Goyal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1480384782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1202793403898392622">Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy by Pawan Mishra is the story of a junior level office worker in India. Known as Coinman due to his habit of never-ending tinkling of coins in his pocket, Kesar is the laughingstock of his office. He even does not find solace in his home as his wife Imli (a passionate actress) completely dissolves herself into different characters on a regular basis. Something unexpected happens when his office colleagues (getting tired and irritated of the continuous jingling of the</span>
  <span id="freeText1202793403898392622" style="display:none">Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy by Pawan Mishra is the story of a junior level office worker in India. Known as Coinman due to his habit of never-ending tinkling of coins in his pocket, Kesar is the laughingstock of his office. He even does not find solace in his home as his wife Imli (a passionate actress) completely dissolves herself into different characters on a regular basis. Something unexpected happens when his office colleagues (getting tired and irritated of the continuous jingling of the coins) come together to conspire against Coinman. This book thus illustrates the permanent plight of an office worker both in home and office due to his eccentricities in a humorous manner. The readers will certainly get impressed by novel’s comedy, its lyricism and its fine intelligence. While the novel will make you laugh, it will also bring a subtle but genuine tragic resonance in your heart. <br /><br />As indicated above, the novel under review is all about Coinman’s personality, life and career. Even the title of the book is an unmistakable pointer of the basic theme of this book. Coinman’s plight evokes not only our sympathy but his character also wins our heart. His becoming Coinman is itself symptomatic of his identity crisis. The past events of Coinman’s life have been woven brilliantly. The author handles the shifting surfaces of past and present with extraordinary fineness and delicacy, and produces a controlled but intricate narrative structure. Even the rest of the characters leave a long lasting impression on your heart. All these characters are easy to identify with. The author has also paid enough attention to name the different chapters. The names of these chapters go well with the flow of the story-line. <br /> <br />The most striking aspect of the comedy in the novel under review is its apparently bottomless and amazingly diverse fund of linguistic humour of all possible kinds. This sense of humour, according to me, deserves all high praises. The style in which the characters of this book speak can only be described as a well of English well-defiled or a verbal version of the Indian rope trick. In other words, it is a brilliant linguistic muddle and a stunning display of stylistic somersaults. The style of the novel is an intricate mosaic fashioned with care. The author employs different speech patterns for different characters and this makes these characters memorable. The characters often lard their speech with jargon drawn from an astonishingly wide range of human thought and activity. And, most importantly, this jargon does not trouble you or irritate you. On the other hand, it keeps bringing smile on your face. You will be amazed to read the speech patterns and word-plays of different characters of this book. These speech patterns are alone worth reading. <br /><br />This book is certainly unlike any other I have read so far and I am delighted that I chose to read this. In fact, I am finding it difficult to describe the beauty of this book in words. I would just say that the book under review is a fun-filled laughing ride and will force readers keep laughing. <br /><br />A must read for all. Go for it! <br /><br />Note: This review was originally posted on <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://pgalmora.wordpress.com/2016/03/30/the-adventures-of-coinman/">https://pgalmora.wordpress.com/2016/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1202793403898392622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14870731954599101444" style="display:none">This hilarious and often insightful and interesting book, follows the story of Coinman, a guy with a habit he can't seem to break. Wherever he is, he's always with his hands in his pockets, listening to the sound of the money. His glamorous actress wife finds her husband's vice incredibly annoying, to the point where she prohibits coins from being brought into their home. As their ridiculous behavior gets the attention of the Coinman's colleagues from work, it changes them in different ways and what follows is completely unexpected.<br /><br />Original, imaginative and full of India's culture, <i>Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy</i> is a book that will stay with you long after you've finished reading it. The characters are creative and realistic, the scenery is vibrantly-described and it's one that you'll never forget.</span>

<div id="review_1442479155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442479155" />
    <a title="Ritu Mishra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48982755-ritu-mishra"><img alt="Ritu Mishra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447512863p2/48982755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1442479155?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ritu Mishra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ritu Mishra" href="/user/show/48982755-ritu-mishra">Ritu Mishra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48982755-ritu-mishra?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48982755-ritu-mishra?shelf=satire">satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48982755-ritu-mishra?shelf=indian-literature">indian-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48982755-ritu-mishra?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48982755-ritu-mishra?shelf=asian-american">asian-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48982755-ritu-mishra?shelf=indian">indian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1442479155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12890910517913646620">Sharing the review from SPR:<br/><br/>Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy by Pawan Mishra is a quirky, heartfelt novel about finding your identity – and keeping it.<br/><br/>The search for personal fulfillment is a lifelong journey for most, and along the way, it is necessary to establish the identity you want, the work you cherish, the people you respect, and the love you deserve. In Pawan Mishra’s oddly charming novel, readers are welcomed into the strangely neurotic, passionate, and unfulfilled existence of Coinman, a</span>
  <span id="freeText12890910517913646620" style="display:none">Sharing the review from SPR:<br /><br />Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy by Pawan Mishra is a quirky, heartfelt novel about finding your identity – and keeping it.<br /><br />The search for personal fulfillment is a lifelong journey for most, and along the way, it is necessary to establish the identity you want, the work you cherish, the people you respect, and the love you deserve. In Pawan Mishra’s oddly charming novel, readers are welcomed into the strangely neurotic, passionate, and unfulfilled existence of Coinman, a simple office worker with a jangling passion for coins.<br /><br />The title of the book suggests this slightly odd premise, but the majority of the book is actually a “day in the life” look at a humble Indian man trying to make his way through a rather extraordinary world.<br /><br />The author raises the banality of normal life to new heights within this novel, and does so in an amusing and thought-provoking way. Office pranks and casual crushes are depicted in epic fashion, while simple conversations, glances, or offhand comments are pulled apart and analyzed by the author’s tireless narration. This offers room throughout the story for social commentary about the dull pain of dead-end jobs, casual betrayal, the evolution of marriage, two-faced friends, the fear of aging parents, and other less common emotional issues of adulthood.<br /><br />This book is largely character-driven, and the author gradually reveals the internal mechanics and daily madness of Coinman from different perspectives, slowly earning him the empathy and understanding of readers. The different points of view used within the story also show the author’s ability to inhabit a variety of characters, and tell a comprehensive tale that can be appreciated from all angles.<br /><br />Readers are invited to peek in on rather ordinary scenes of Coinman’s domestic and professional life, and experience the detailed struggles of adult life from all sides. As readers begin to understand the diverse contexts in which Coinman exists, they inevitably see more of themselves in the character. He is not a bumbling fool, nor is he deserving of the mockery and wrath of his co-workers or wife. He is merely a man doing his best to survive without compromising the things he cares about, or the identity he works hard to cultivate.<br /><br />The search for identity and comfort in one’s own skin dominates many of the short vignettes and interactions between characters, and is particularly strong in the character of Imli, Coinman’s wife. Her theatrical roles come to define her life, from playing a ghost and abandoning all mortal possessions, to acting as a jealous wife who suspects her husband of adultery with the maid. She is a chameleon in every sense of the word, deriving meaning and purpose from the masks she wears, and forcing Coinman to temporarily inhabit those worlds alongside her. This is starkly contrary to Coinman, who seems determined to find pleasure in his own strange brand of life, yet also remains endlessly devoted to his unusual partner.<br /><br />This is far from an action-packed book, namely because the author tends to use narration a bit too much, not allowing characters to speak their minds, but rather utilizing internal monologues and heavy exposition throughout the story. This can get a bit much at times, but this is also Mishra’s time to flex his literary and descriptive muscles.<br /><br />While the author’s native language is clearly not English, the slightly odd dialect of the dialogue makes it a more endearing and authentic story, and isn’t as distracting as one might expect. A steady editorial hand would have also helped with some of the more disjointed scenes, and suggested where the plot could be strengthened (or cut down). Despite its occasional failings, the story is uniquely enjoyable, and Coinman is a character that will be hard to forget.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.selfpublishingreview.com/2016/03/review-coinman-by-pawan-mishra/">http://www.selfpublishingreview.com/2...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12890910517913646620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1633030687" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Punya Nayak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19535800-punya-nayak"><img alt="Punya Nayak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466923196p2/19535800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1633030687?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Punya Nayak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Punya Nayak" href="/user/show/19535800-punya-nayak">Punya Nayak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19535800-punya-nayak?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19535800-punya-nayak?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19535800-punya-nayak?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1633030687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2916984665457697396">Thanks to the author, Pawan Mishra, and the publisher,Lune Spark LLC, for providing me with a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. I feel completely grateful that I was given the opportunity to read this, even if it is not one of my preferred genres and to find that I actually love it!<br/><br/>Coinman is the story of <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Kesar, <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, who has an obsession with jingling coins in his pocket. However this bad habit drives his peers into hating him. Soon he is isolated and</span>
  <span id="freeText2916984665457697396" style="display:none">Thanks to the author, Pawan Mishra, and the publisher,Lune Spark LLC, for providing me with a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. I feel completely grateful that I was given the opportunity to read this, even if it is not one of my preferred genres and to find that I actually love it!<br /><br />Coinman is the story of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kesar, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, who has an obsession with jingling coins in his pocket. However this bad habit drives his peers into hating him. Soon he is isolated and becomes the scapegoat for gossip mongers. His peers begin to call him by the name "coinman" which causes him to lose of his identity. Thus our mighty hero becomes an office stooge, the butt of many jokes. <br /><br />I can honestly say that this book is unlike any other I have read before, a breath of fresh air. The writing is superb and the characters are different. I loved the sardonic and humorous tone. I immensely enjoyed the Indianized style in which the characters of this book speak. The story felt strangely relateable because I felt that this book was a exaggerated version of exactly what happens in my college. Despite being a very unlikable character, I found myself favoring coinman because of how he treated others. The plot is simple, but it offers different perspectives and home and work life of multiple characters. One of the strengths of this book was that its timeline dipped between present and the past and the author has done this brilliantly. This book is one of the few Indian novels where it doesn't contain the same old romance cliche with sex thrown in to make it crispy. <br /><br />What confused me about this book was that it is narrated by an unrelated character called Sesha which felt unnecessary. I might have missed something. But it left me frustrated to understand the story for the first few pages. <br /><br />Concluding I would like to say that this is a wonderful book and makes you believe different or odd doesn’t always mean bad. <br /><br />Highlighted quotes:<br />1. “You can make any promises as long as you are not going to be there to fulfill them.” <br />2. “With the wolves around, your humbleness is your worst adversary.” <br />3. “Disappointment has quite a penchant for taking one by a surprise.” <br />4.“As soon as anger knocks at one’s door, wisdom prepares to leave.” </span>
  <a data-text-id="2916984665457697396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17195942094204210980" style="display:none">I received an audible copy of this book from the publisher in exchange for a fair review.<br /><br />Actual rating: 3.5<br /><br />Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy is beautifully written and the story is nothing like what I've encountered before. The story revolves around a man with OCD who likes to jingle coins in his pocket, so his coworkers nickname him Coinman. The group of people he works with constantly gossip about him, spread rumors, mock him and pull pranks on him... basically bullying him. Coinman doesn't have the easiest life at home either, with a wife obsessed with her own well-being, and a mother obsessed with making her son's marriage successful, the man can't catch a break.<br />I was really close to giving it more stars but something kept haunting me: this book is marketed as humor. And while it is filled with humorous elements, I was too frustrated by the behavior of all the co-workers to really focus on the satire.<br />But I still recommend it. It's an amazing read.</span>

<div id="review_1566401848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566401848" />
    <a title="Heena Rathore P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19253213-heena-rathore-p"><img alt="Heena Rathore P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597647146p2/19253213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1566401848?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heena Rathore P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heena Rathore P." href="/user/show/19253213-heena-rathore-p">Heena Rathore P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19253213-heena-rathore-p?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19253213-heena-rathore-p?shelf=review-requests">review-requests</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19253213-heena-rathore-p?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19253213-heena-rathore-p?shelf=indian-authors">indian-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1566401848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer946246349717263327"><b>Note:</b> I received a copy of this book from the author in exchange for an honest review. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>"It all began with high expectations."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I rarely read literary fiction but when I was presented with an opportunity to read Coinman I thought of giving this one a try as the author is a fellow Indian. Though initially I had a few reservations about reading it, this book turned out to be a really interesting one. Coinman is a really unique read about a man who is obsessed with jingling coins.<br/><br/>Author Pawan Mish</span>
  <span id="freeText946246349717263327" style="display:none"><b>Note:</b> I received a copy of this book from the author in exchange for an honest review. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"It all began with high expectations."</i>
</b><br /><br />I rarely read literary fiction but when I was presented with an opportunity to read Coinman I thought of giving this one a try as the author is a fellow Indian. Though initially I had a few reservations about reading it, this book turned out to be a really interesting one. Coinman is a really unique read about a man who is obsessed with jingling coins.<br /><br />Author Pawan Mishra has done a great job writing about a character as bizarre as Coinman and that too with dollops of sarcastic and classy humor blending it brilliantly with the main conflict of the story.<br /><br />Though I'm not a huge fan of literary fiction, this book was fairly good and I enjoyed reading it. At times, I was chuckling loudly making everyone around me uncomfortable... so you can imagine how much I enjoyed it.<br /><br />This book cleverly explores the day-to-day problems, faced by people who are termed as different or socially awkward by the seemingly "normal" people or the people who proudly calls themselves as extroverts, with a fine layer of sarcasm and wit to make the reading a really pleasant experience. It also covers the issue of bullying, which, I'm sure, will make many heads nod.<br /><br />Overall it is a brilliant read and I'd recommend it to everyone as there are a lot of other social themes which will appeal to the masses.<br /><br />You can also read this review at <b><a href="http://www.thereadingbud.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Reading Bud</a>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="946246349717263327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1762213069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1762213069" />
    <a title="Davyne DeSye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49054501-davyne-desye"><img alt="Davyne DeSye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538613956p2/49054501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1762213069?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Davyne DeSye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Davyne DeSye" href="/user/show/49054501-davyne-desye">Davyne DeSye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1762213069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5587201555821512176">This was a very quirky, satiric look at office politics and their often ridiculous nature.<br/><br/>The main character is Coinman, a nickname given him because of his constant habit of jingling coins in his pocket – a habit that drives all of his co-workers absolutely insane. I really enjoyed his character at the same time that I often felt sorry for him. I also enjoyed the exaggerated nature of everything – Tulsi’s beauty, Ratiram’s wisdom and, of course, Coinman’s habit itself. I also liked the glimpses</span>
  <span id="freeText5587201555821512176" style="display:none">This was a very quirky, satiric look at office politics and their often ridiculous nature.<br /><br />The main character is Coinman, a nickname given him because of his constant habit of jingling coins in his pocket – a habit that drives all of his co-workers absolutely insane. I really enjoyed his character at the same time that I often felt sorry for him. I also enjoyed the exaggerated nature of everything – Tulsi’s beauty, Ratiram’s wisdom and, of course, Coinman’s habit itself. I also liked the glimpses into Indian culture. The mystique that surrounded ABC and the “disappearance” of office employees after a meeting with the three dreaded figures was hilarious. I’d want to be asked to retire!<br /><br />I must admit to being a little disappointed by the end, but I suppose I shouldn’t be because Coinman’s life is destined to be so much better. On the other hand, I will miss Coinman’s quirkiness.<br /><br />This book takes the reader on an odd journey… If you are looking for a straightforward book told in a straightforward manner, this book is not for you. If, on the other hand, you are in the mood for hyperbole, (sometimes odd, sometimes profound) philosophy and digressions that are mini stories in themselves, this book will definitely hit the spot!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5587201555821512176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1576889528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18081935819528166858">I received this book for free via Goodreads First Reads.<br/><br/>I sometimes finish a book and think I have never read a book like it before. That was definitely the case here.<br/><br/>The main theme for a lot of the book is bullying. Both in the workplace and domestically. It is interesting that the main character is never portrayed as weak despite the fact he is bullied. The supporting characters maybe could have been fleshed out a little more but the titular character is fascinating enough to make up for this.</span>
  <span id="freeText18081935819528166858" style="display:none">I received this book for free via Goodreads First Reads.<br /><br />I sometimes finish a book and think I have never read a book like it before. That was definitely the case here.<br /><br />The main theme for a lot of the book is bullying. Both in the workplace and domestically. It is interesting that the main character is never portrayed as weak despite the fact he is bullied. The supporting characters maybe could have been fleshed out a little more but the titular character is fascinating enough to make up for this.<br /><br />I enjoyed the story and it has enough sub-plots to keep it going. I think certain plot points deserved a conclusion but I wonder if the author has a sequel in mind. <br /><br />My only real gripe about the book is some scenes and conversations seem slightly overwritten. It feels like the author tried to hard to fill some spaces (which a lot of new authors do). This is just an observation that I make quite often when I review a book and it did not spoil my enjoyment of the words.<br /><br />I would recommend it to people who are looking for something a bit different. I enjoyed the read and I am sure a lot of other people do. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18081935819528166858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8783847-ginger-bensman?shelf=parable-fiction">parable-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1698011209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8175100197480973254">This story is a modern day parable. Coinman, Mishra’s protagonist, is often hapless, frequently pathetic, and always likeable. His seemingly harmless compulsion to finger the coins in his pocket leads to chaos at work (he’s singled out, harassed and brutally bullied by his colleagues), and there’s trouble in his marriage (he is henpecked and abused by his ridiculously self-centered wife). The Coinman’s troubles take place in India and the prose reflects an Indian sensibility and cadence. If the </span>
  <span id="freeText8175100197480973254" style="display:none">This story is a modern day parable. Coinman, Mishra’s protagonist, is often hapless, frequently pathetic, and always likeable. His seemingly harmless compulsion to finger the coins in his pocket leads to chaos at work (he’s singled out, harassed and brutally bullied by his colleagues), and there’s trouble in his marriage (he is henpecked and abused by his ridiculously self-centered wife). The Coinman’s troubles take place in India and the prose reflects an Indian sensibility and cadence. If the novel has a fault, it’s that Mishra dwells overlong on certain aspects of the story, for instance, I thought scenes that elaborated Coinman’s penchant for coin-jingling could have been pared back to good effect. Coinman: An Untold Conspiracy, is laced with psychological insight, pithy wisdom (e.g. “a man in pain is more likely to take refuge in telling the truth”), and is an astute parody of the dynamics of office politics and “group think.” (4.5 stars rounded to 5)<br /></span>

<div id="review_1700999683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1700999683" />
    <a title="Merril Anil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20903756-merril-anil"><img alt="Merril Anil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409817585p2/20903756.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1700999683?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merril Anil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merril Anil" href="/user/show/20903756-merril-anil">Merril Anil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20903756-merril-anil?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20903756-merril-anil?shelf=author-s-handdown">author-s-handdown</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1700999683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16626119123052182354"><b> its massively twisted and coiled </b><br/><br/><i> First of all a huge thanks to the author for providing me with a copy of the book to read and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kavita Ramesh </a> for recommending me to the author though i am sure after reading this he wouldn't be too happy about it :( and you probably would want to hide to save yourself from the wrath of the author and let me know where you plan to hide so that i can join you as well. :P </i><br/><br/>I admit that the book is a lot different and definitely stands unique from its contemporaries</span>
  <span id="freeText16626119123052182354" style="display:none"><b> its massively twisted and coiled </b><br><br><i> First of all a huge thanks to the author for providing me with a copy of the book to read and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Kavita Ramesh </a> for recommending me to the author though i am sure after reading this he wouldn't be too happy about it :( and you probably would want to hide to save yourself from the wrath of the author and let me know where you plan to hide so that i can join you as well. :P </i><br><br>I admit that the book is a lot different and definitely stands unique from its contemporaries but perhaps I am not the right audience that this book was targeted to either that or the concerns I had with the book was indeed true.<br><br>The language of the book is so twisted that I felt that if I pick a sentence of the book, it could easily be broken and dissected to form an entire paragraph because each sentence had things worth an entire paragraph rolled into one.<br><br>What happens with such kind of narration is that by the time one finishes a sentence you feel you have read almost an entire chapter yet nothing has registered in your mind because you were trying to find out meaning of each word that you lost the bigger picture<br><br>The author sadly gets caught up in bringing out events after events that the actual track sort of derails. The author unfortunately also gets lured in background details a little too much. Ironically there is a sequence in the book where couple of characters gather around to hear latest gossip from their local gossip supplier and the guy is so distracted and busy narrating the background details that the other characters starts getting angry at him for not coming straight to the point and wasting time and trying on their patience . Funny enough that I thought this was exactly what was happening to the actual book<br><br>I also suspect that the book got run over by a thesaurus truck because at same places things don't even make sense because of the Wrong synonyms taking place and changing the full meaning of the sentence.<br><br>Now that I have been saying bad things let me come to good points. I noticed that the author had used very unique and different similes and phrases ... Quite unusual and unheard ones and that definitely was pretty interesting and charming. There are portions where individually each line is amazing but when put together with the rest, it sort of fails to sit well with the context but still there are some really poetic and erudite lines in the book<br><br><b> I guess I was the wrong audience for the book because for me personally the language was a tough one to crack for being really twisty and running long and most importantly the book got drowned in background details too much that it turned out difficult for me to pick out the main plot in the book but when I eventually did, I was actually impressed with how one little personality trait was used by the author to weave a complete story. Wish the author had simplified the treatment of the plot a bit more for the ease of a wider audience </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469383363ra/19812446.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16626119123052182354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553204630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16937240062488616946">Review from IndieReader (with a 5 star rating):<br/><br/>Social commentary highlighted through a curmudgeon’s antics in: COINMAN<br/><br/>"This articulate, wryly amusing creation focuses on simple situations that often have an unexpected, almost magical, twist."<br/><br/>The anti-hero known as “Coinman” is an irritating co-worker, an inattentive husband, a not-so-dutiful son…yet his apparent lack of love conquers all.<br/><br/>Coinman (his real name is Kesar) gets his nickname for his disturbing habit of constantly jingling coins that</span>
  <span id="freeText16937240062488616946" style="display:none">Review from IndieReader (with a 5 star rating):<br /><br />Social commentary highlighted through a curmudgeon’s antics in: COINMAN<br /><br />"This articulate, wryly amusing creation focuses on simple situations that often have an unexpected, almost magical, twist."<br /><br />The anti-hero known as “Coinman” is an irritating co-worker, an inattentive husband, a not-so-dutiful son…yet his apparent lack of love conquers all.<br /><br />Coinman (his real name is Kesar) gets his nickname for his disturbing habit of constantly jingling coins that “occupied an eternal place in the left pocket of his trousers and…constantly slithered through the narrow space between his fingers.” Driven nuts by this annoying quirk, his coworkers begin slowly inching their desks away from him, a tactic that Coinman counters by measuring the progress of their retreat with tape and markers. They then instigate a series of increasingly hostile pranks designed to get him fired.<br /><br />Set in India, COINMAN is narrated by Sesha, a storyteller who interjects his commentary at the beginning and end. The novel’s office scenes satisfyingly satirize the inner workings of a tight-knit bureaucracy: the irrelevant meetings, the arbitrary policies, the workers’ fears of management. But it is not only at work that Coinman’s odd personality arouses concern. His mother worries that he will never find a wife. When he finally does, his bride spends the first few weeks of their marriage weeping ceaselessly, then turns her attention to her own pursuit—the theater—having accepted that Coinman is not interested in producing offspring.<br /><br />For all its darker aspects, this episodic work is curiously lighthearted, concluding on a positive note, with the bureaucracy working for, rather than against Coinman, and the subtle intervention of a famous guru working mystically on his marriage.<br /><br />The author of this gentle parody of human frailty, Pawan Mishra, is an Indian residing in the US who states in a Foreword that his love of folktales began in childhood, hearing older relatives tell “bedtime stories that were never written down.” This articulate, wryly amusing creation focuses on simple situations that often have an unexpected, almost magical, twist. Mishra has taken what could have been a tragic tale of bullying, workplace harassment, even violence, and deftly transmuted it into a droll parable. In COINMAN, he has fashioned an archetypal folk hero who, seemingly oblivious to the criticism and opposition all around him, gets his way as it had been planned all along.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16937240062488616946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1551709178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1551709178" />
    <a title="Snehal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6350736-snehal"><img alt="Snehal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562940806p2/6350736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1551709178?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Snehal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Snehal" href="/user/show/6350736-snehal">Snehal</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1551709178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12790499201252340440">I received this book to review as part of a Goodreads initiative. The synopsis of the book appealed to me as it is set in an office environment and my background in human resources and organisational behaviour added more fuel to the metaphorical fire. <br/><br/>The protagonist of the book is a chap called Coinman, your average office goer who finds himself at the brunt of office politics and a victim of bullying behaviour. It was difficult for me to not classify the various miseries that Coinman faces as </span>
  <span id="freeText12790499201252340440" style="display:none">I received this book to review as part of a Goodreads initiative. The synopsis of the book appealed to me as it is set in an office environment and my background in human resources and organisational behaviour added more fuel to the metaphorical fire. <br /><br />The protagonist of the book is a chap called Coinman, your average office goer who finds himself at the brunt of office politics and a victim of bullying behaviour. It was difficult for me to not classify the various miseries that Coinman faces as gross misconduct on part of the perpetrators (Yes, my HR hat remained tightly secured). <br /><br />The book is based in a small city in North India and the characters that you come across are easy to identify if you have worked in a small private ltd company in India e.g. the loyal employee with an unreasonable sense of entitlement, a clique of 3 to 4 employees who dare not deviate from group norms, an ‘off-handish’ manager, a female employee who is the ‘heartthrob’ of every male employee solely because of her perceived film star looks and last but not the least, senior management who only make an appearance to reprimand or fire someone. <br /><br />I couldn’t help but empathise with the protagonist and wanted him to succeed against the bullies in each cruel situation. Although the plot was well thought through, I felt that the use of language left much to be desired. Having said that, I will give the benefit of doubt to the author as this may have been done intentionally in order to be in sync with the characters and the setting. There are many Hindi terms used in the narrative which gives the reader a good feel for the environment in which the story transpires. A glossary with the terms explained is useful for a reader not familiar with Hindi. <br /><br />My profession dictates that I am alert to the prevalence of bullying in the workplace so I must emphasise that I felt very uncomfortable reading about the details. This doesn’t take away from the fact that this type of behaviour is unfortunately not uncommon in organisations. Therefore, by addressing this often ‘brushed under the carpet’ topic, Mishra has indeed done well. Finally, does the book have a satisfying ending? I’ll let you decide!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12790499201252340440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
